Whitney anukramaс╣З─л

[Atharvan.тАФpa├▒caviс╣Е┼Ыakam. k─Бmadevatyam. tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham: 5. atijagat─л; 7. jagat─л; 8. 2-p. ─Бrc─л pan╠Дkti; 11, 20, 23. bhurij; 12. anuс╣гс╣нubh; 13. 2-p. ─Бrcy anuс╣гс╣нubh; 14, 15, 17, 18, 21, 22. jagat─л; 16. 4-p. ┼Ыakvar─лgarbh─Б par─Бjagat─л.]

Comment

тМКPartly proseтАФ“vs.” 13.тМЛ Found also (except vs. 4) in P─Бipp. xvi. тМКwith vs. 16 before 12 and vs. 24 before 20тМЛ. The hymn (vs. 1) is prescribed in V─Бit. 24. 10 to be recited, with homage to K─Бma, in a part of the Agniс╣гс╣нoma ceremony; and in K─Бu┼Ы. 49. 1 it (vs. 1) accompanies the release of a bull in a witchcraft ceremony.

Translations

Translated: Muir, v. 404 (nearly all); Ludwig, p. 519; Scherman, Philosophische Hymnen, p. 76 (part); Henry, 84, 118; Griffith, i. 430; Bloomfield, 220, 591.тАФCf. Hillebrandt, Veda-Chrestomathie, p. 40.

Griffith

A glorification of Kama as God of desire of all that is good

режрез рд╕рдкрддреНрдирд╣рдирдореГрд╖рднрдВ рдШреГрддреЗрди ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. The rival-slaying bull K─Бma do I desire to aid (? ┼Ыikс╣г) with ghee,
    with oblation, with sacrificial butter; do thou, praised with great
    heroism, make my rivals to fall downward.
Notes

K─Бma, lit. ‘desire, love,’ is so thoroughly personified throughout the
hymn that the word is better transferred than translated.

Griffith

Kama the Bull, slayer of foes, I worship with molten butter, sacrifice, oblation. Beneath my feet cast down mine adversaries with thy great manly power, when I have praised thee.

режреи рдпрдиреНрдореЗ рдордирд╕реЛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. What of my mind or my sight is not agreeable (priy├б), what of me
    gnaws, does not enjoy (abhi-nand), that evil-dreaming do I fasten on
    my rival; praising K─Бma, may I shoot up.
Notes

The sense of a, b is very doubtful; without b added, a would
naturally mean ‘what is not agreeable to my mind or sight’; the Pet.
Lex. proposes to help the difficulty rather by emending b to yasm─Бd
b─лbhatse yac ca n─Б тАЩbhinande. This verse and the following one are
included in the duс╕еsvapnan─Б┼Ыana gaс╣Зa: see note to K─Бu┼Ы. 46. 9. There
is an irregularity in every p─Бda, but the Anukr. does not heed them.
Ppp. has, for b, yan me hс╣Ыdaye na тАЩbhinandanti; and, for d,
k─Бmaс╣Б juс╣гс╣нa h─Бnudaс╣Б bhideyamтАФthus giving us no help. тМКPischel treats
the vs., Ved. Stud. ii. 61. Aufrecht, KZ. xxxiv. 459, sees here a root
bhas ‘verdriessen, taedere.’тМЛ

Griffith

That which is hateful to mine eye and spirit, that harasses and robs me of enjoyment, The evil dream I loose upon my foemen. May I rend him when I have lauded Kama.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Evil-dreaming, O K─Бma, and difficulty, O K─Бma, want of progeny,
    homelessness, ruin do thou, formidable, masterful, fasten on him who
    shall seek to devise (cikits-) distresses for us.
Notes

Ppp. combines yo тАШsmabhyam in d.

Griffith

Kama, do thou, a mighty Lord and Ruler, let loose ill dream, misfortune, want of children, Homelessness, Kama! utter destitution, upon the sinner who designs my ruin.

режрек рдиреБрджрд╕реНрд╡ рдХрд╛рдо ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Thrust, O K─Бma; thrust forth, O K─Бma; let them who are my rivals go
    to ruin; of them, thrust to lowest darknesses, do thou, O Agni, burn out
    the abodes (v─Б╠Бstu).
Notes

The Anukr. takes no notice of the deficiency of two syllables in d,
which in 9 d is made up by the addition of anu. In V─Бit. 4. 5 the
verse is strangely used to accompany the separation of two sacrificial
ladles; in K─Бu┼Ы. 48. 5 it accompanies the driving away of something with
a branch.

Griffith

Drive them away, drive them afar, O Kama; indigence fall on those who are my foemen! When they have been cast down to deepest darkness, consume their dwellings with thy fire, O Agni.

режрел рд╕рд╛ рддреЗ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. That daughter of thine, O K─Бma, is called a milch-cow, what utterance
    (v─Б╠Бc) the poets name vir─Б╠Бj; with that do thou avoid them that are my
    rivals; let breath, cattle, life avoid them.
Notes

Or a might be ’that milch-cow is called thy daughter.’ O. reads
p├бry eс╣З─Бn in d; but the passage is quoted under Pr─Бt. iii. 80 as
one in which the lingualization of n does not take place.

Griffith

She, Kama! she is called the Cow, thy daughter, she who is named Vak and Viraj by sages. By her drive thou my foemen to a distance. May cattle, vital breath, and life forsake them.

Translation
  1. With the strength of K─Бma, of Indra, of king Varuс╣Зa, of Vishс╣Зu, with
    the impulse of Savitar (’the impeller’), with the priestship (hotr├б)
    of Agni I thrust forth my rivals, as a skilful pole-man (? ┼Ыamb├нn) a
    boat on the waters (udak├б).
Notes

┼Ыamb├нn occurs nowhere else, and the meaning of ┼Ы├бmba is doubtful.
Ppp. reads in c pi┼Ы─Бc─Бn instead of sapatn─Бn.

Griffith

By Kama’s might, King Varuna’s and Indra’s, by Vishnu’s strength, and Savitar’s instigation, I chase my foes with sacrifice to Agni, as a deft steersman drives his boat through waters.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let K─Бma, my valiant (v─Бj├нn) formidable overseer, make for me
    freedom from rivals; let the all-gods be my refuge; let all the gods
    come to this call of mine.
Notes

‘All’ is v├н┼Ыve in c, and s├бrve in d. The verse is called
jagat─л by the Anukr., though only d is a jagat─л p─Бda тМКand that
only by countтМЛ. Ppp. combines at the end of d m─Бi тАЩmam тМКand thus
suggests the true metrical rendering of d as a triс╣гс╣нubh: similarly
at ix. 3. 15тМЛ.

Griffith

May Kama, mighty one, my potent warder, give me full free- dom from mine adversaries. May all the Deities be my protection, all Gods come nigh to this mine invocation.

  1. Becoming, O K─Бma, in alliance (sar├бtham) with Indra-and-Agni, may
    ye make my rivals to fall downward; of them, fallen to lowest
    darknesses, do thou, O Agni, burn along out the abodes.
Notes

With c, d compare 4 c, d above. The first half-verse presents
various anomalies: sar├бtham demands an instrumental case; we should
expect rather a plural verb (but compare vi. 104. 3 a, b); and it
should be accented after h├н. Emending indr─Бgn─л╠Б to ├нndreс╣Зa, and
reading p─Бd├бy─Бthas, would make everything right.

Griffith

Ye, Indra, Agni, Kama! come together and cast mine adver- saries down beneath me. When they have sunk into the deepest darkness, O Agni, with thy fire consume their dwellings.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Slay thou, O K─Бma, those that are my rivals; make them fall down to
    blind darknesses; be they all senseless (? n├нrindriya), sapless; let
    them not live any day soever.
Notes

Ppp. combines sapatn─Б тАЩndh─Б in a-b, combines and reads nirindriy─Б
тАЩrav─Бс╕е in c, and has for d yath─Б nu j─лv─Бt katamac тМК-ma┼Ы?тМЛ
cane тАЩс╣г─Бс╣Б.

Griffith

Slay those who are mine enemies, O Kama: headlong to depth of blinding darkness hurl them. Reft be they all of manly strength and vigour! Let them not have a single day’s existence.

Whitney
Translation
  1. K─Бma hath slain (vadh) them that are my rivals; he hath made for
    me wide space, prosperity; let the four directions bow to me; let the
    six wide ones тМКfem.тМЛ bring ghee to me.
Notes

The third p─Бda was found above as v. 3. 1 c. It is unusual for the
Anukr. to note as bhurij a triс╣гс╣нubh containing a *jagat─л-*p─Бda. тМКCf.
Bergaigne, Rel. V├йd. ii. 122.тМЛ

Griffith

Kama hath slain those who were mine opponents, and given me ample room to grow and prosper. Let the four regions bow them down before me, and let the six expanses bring me fatness.

  1. Let them float away downward, like a boat severed from its mooring;
    of them, thrust forth by missiles, there is no return again.

Griffith

Let them drift downward like a boat torn from the rope that held it fast. There is no turning back for those whom our keen arrows have repelled.

yavayanty amum amuс╣гy─Бyaс╣Зam amuс╣гy─Бс╣г putraс╣Б j─лvalokaс╣Б mс╣Ыtalokaс╣Б kat─Б

dvyavas─Бn─Б.

Translation
  1. With his heroes not safe тМК├б-sarvav─лraтМЛ let him go on, thrust
    forth, to be hated of friends, to be avoided of his own kin; on earth
    also stay (ava-s─Б) thunderbolts; may the formidable god massacre your
    rivals.
Notes

The sense of c is obscure; vidy├║tas might also be object of the
verb: ’they let loose thunderbolts.’ Ppp. puts dveс╣гyas after
mitr─Бс╣З─Бm in b. The Anukr. calls the verse a jagat─л, although it
is a triс╣гс╣нubh with one jagat─л-p─Бda (like 11). тМКW. usually renders
s├бrvav─лra by ‘with all [his, our, etc.] heroes.’тМЛ

Griffith

To be avoided by his friends, detested, repelled, with few men round him, let him wander. Yea, on the earth descend the lightning-flashes: may the strong God destroy your adversaries.

резрел рдЪреНрдпреБрддрд╛ рдЪреЗрдпрдореН ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. This great [earth], both stirred and unstirred, bears the
    lightning and all the thunders; let the ─Аditya, arising with property,
    with brilliancy, thrust downward my rivals, he the powerful one.
Notes

The first half-verse is wholly obscure, and the version given commits
the grammatical solecism of taking vidy├║t as neut. accus. But for the
last ca, vidyut might be taken as subject of the sentence. The verse
has a triс╣гс╣нubh-p─Бda (a), of which the Anukr. makes no account.

Griffith

This potent lightning nourishes things shaken, and things un- shaken yet, and all the thunders. May the Sun, rising with his wealth and splendour, drive in victorious might my foemen downward.

Translation
  1. What sufficient (udbh├║) triply-guarding defense thou hast, O K─Бma,
    worship (br├бhman) as extended protection (v├бrman), made
    unpierceable, with that do thou avoid them that are my rivals; let
    breath, cattle, life avoid them.

The last half-verse is тМКnearlyтМЛ identical with 5 c, d above, and O.
again reads eс╣З─Бn in d. Ppp. puts the verse next before our 12. The
description of the meter by the Anukr. is unintelligible, since we have
(12 + 14: 12 + 14) 52 syllables, or an atijagat─л; perhaps par─Бjagat─л
is a misreading for this.

Griffith

Thy firm and triply-barred protection, Kama! thy spell, made weapon-proof extended armour With that drive thou my foemen to a distance. May cattle, vital breath, and life forsake them.

Whitney
Translation
  1. As the gods thrust forth the Asuras, as Indra drove (b─Бdh) the
    barbarians to lowest darkness, so do thou, O K─Бma, thrust forth far from
    this world those who are my rivals.
Notes

Ppp. has again tamo тАШpab─Бdhe, but this time d┼лram. The “jagat─л”
meter is like that of vs. 17.

Griffith

As Gods repelled the Asuras, and Indra down to the lowest darkness drove the demons, So, Kama, from this world, to distant places, drive thou the men who are mine adversaries.

Translation
  1. K─Бma was first born; not the gods, the Fathers, nor mortals attained

no тАЩta marty─Бс╕е; and it combines in d nam─Бi тАЩt. The verse (9 тМК10?тМЛ

  • 10: 12 + 11 = 42) is a queer “triс╣гс╣нubh.”
Griffith

First before all sprang Kama into being. Gods, Fathers, mortal men have never matched him. Stronger than these art thou, and great for ever. Kama, to thee, to thee I offer worship.

Griffith

Vast as the quarters of the sky and regions that lie between them spread in all directions, vast as celestial tracts and views of heaven, Stronger than these art thou, and great for ever. Kama, to thee, to thee I offer worship.

Translation
  1. How many the humble-bees (bhс╣Ы╠Бn╠Дga), the bats, the kur┼л╠Бnus; how
    many have been the v├бgh─Бs, the tree-creepersтАФto them art thou etc.
    etc.
Notes

The verse is a jagat─л in number of syllables (12 + 13: 12 + 11 = 48).
Bp. accents jatv├бс╕е in a.

Griffith

Many as are the bees, and bats, and reptiles, and female serpents of the trees, and beetles, Stronger art thou than these, and great for ever. Kama, to thee, to thee I offer worship.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What propitious excellent bodies thou hast, O K─Бma, with which what
    thou choosest becometh real, with them do thou enter wholly into us;
    make evil devices (dh─л╠Б) enter away elsewhere.
Notes

The combination t─Б╠Бbhiс╣г с╣нv├бm is an example under Pr─Бt. ii. 84, and is
quoted in the commentary there. Ppp. reads vс╣Ыс╣З─лte at end of b,
upa- for abhi- in c, and upa for apa in d. The Anukr.
pays no heed to the extra syllable in d. The verse is quoted in
K─Бu┼Ы. 24. 29 in the ─Бgrah─Бyaс╣З─л ceremony, to accompany the act of lying
down (apparently merely on account of the occurrence of -saс╣Б-vi┼Ы in
c).

тМКThe quoted Anukr. here says k─Бmas┼лktaс╕е.тМЛ

тМКHere ends the first anuv─Бka, with 2 hymns and 49 verses.тМЛ

Griffith

Thy lovely and auspicious forms, O Kama, whereby the thing thou wilt becometh real, With these come thou and make thy home among us, and make malignant thoughts inhabit elsewhere.
